Four concrete backends implement this interface:\\n\\n1. **GCP Cloud KMS** (internal/encryption/cloudkms/cloud_kms.go): Uses Google Cloud KMS API with envelope encryption — a random AES-256 key encrypts the payload, then KMS wraps that key.\\n2. **AWS KMS** (internal/encryption/awskms/aws_kms.go): Uses AWS KMS API with the same envelope pattern — AES-256 local encryption with the envelope key protected by AWS KMS.\\n3. **Mounted Key** (internal/encryption/mounted/key.go): AES-256-GCM encryption using a 32-byte key loaded from an environment variable or filesystem path. Also uses envelope encryption internally. This is the self-hosted/on-prem option.\\n4. **Noop Key** (internal/encryption/noop.go): A passthrough that stores data unencrypted. Used when no encryption is configured.\\n\\nSupporting primitives:\\n- **aeshelper** (internal/encryption/aeshelper/aeshelper.go): Raw AES-256-GCM encrypt/decrypt.\\n- **envelope** (internal/encryption/envelope/envelope.go): Envelope encryption — generates a random 32-byte key, encrypts plaintext with AES-GCM, returns (key, nonce, ciphertext).\\n- **wrapper** (internal/encryption/wrapper/encryptedvalue.go): Serialization layer — `StorableEncryptedKey` struct (mechanism, key name, wrapped key, ciphertext, nonce) serialized as base64-encoded JSON.\\n- **cache** (internal/encryption/cache/cache.go): Optional LRU cache wrapping any Key to memoize decrypt results, keyed by FNV-64 hash of ciphertext.\\n\\nThe **keyring** (internal/encryption/keyring/ring.go) is the global registry. `Ring` struct holds one `encryption.Key` per sensitive data domain: `BatchChangesCredentialKey`, `ExternalServiceKey`, `GitHubAppKey`, `OutboundWebhookKey`, `UserExternalAccountKey`, `WebhookKey`, `WebhookLogKey`, `ExecutorSecretKey`, `SlackConfigurationKey`. Keys are configured in site config under `encryption.keys` (schema/site.schema.json). `keyring.Init()` watches for config changes and rebuilds the ring; `keyring.Default()` provides global access.\\n\\nApplication code uses `Encryptable` (internal/encryption/encryptable.go) and `JSONEncryptable` (internal/encryption/json_encryptable.go) wrappers, which lazily encrypt/decrypt and memoize results. `MaybeEncrypt`/`MaybeDecrypt` (internal/encryption/helpers.go) are nil-safe helpers: if key is nil, data is stored/returned plaintext — this is the noop/disabled path. A special `ALLOW_DECRYPTION` env var suppresses new encryption while a migration worker decrypts the database.\\n\\nEncrypted **database fields** (cmd/worker/internal/encryption/encryption_tables.go):\\n- `external_services.config` → ExternalServiceKey\\n- `user_external_accounts.auth_data`, `account_data` → UserExternalAccountKey\\n- `user_credentials.credential` → BatchChangesCredentialKey\\n- `batch_changes_site_credentials.credential` → BatchChangesCredentialKey\\n- `webhook_logs.request`, `response` → WebhookLogKey\\n- `executor_secrets.value` → ExecutorSecretKey\\n- `outbound_webhooks.url`, `secret` → OutboundWebhookKey\\n- `slack_configurations.signing_secret`, `bot_token` → SlackConfigurationKey\\n\\nEach encrypted database row stores both the ciphertext and an `encryption_key_id` (serialized KeyVersion JSON) so the system can detect key mismatches on decryption. \"summary\": \"Sourcegraph's encryption-at-rest system is built around the `encryption.Key` interface (internal/encryption/key.go), which defines Encrypt/Decrypt/Version methods. Four concrete backends implement this interface:\\n\\n1. **GCP Cloud KMS** (internal/encryption/cloudkms/cloud_kms.go): Uses Google Cloud KMS API with envelope encryption — a random AES-256 key encrypts the payload locally, then KMS wraps that envelope key.\\n2. **AWS KMS** (internal/encryption/awskms/aws_kms.go): Uses AWS KMS API with the same envelope pattern — AES-256-GCM local encryption with the envelope key protected by AWS KMS.\\n3. **Mounted Key** (internal/encryption/mounted/key.go): AES-256-GCM encryption using a 32-byte key loaded from an environment variable or filesystem path. Uses envelope encryption internally. This is the self-hosted/on-prem option.\\n4. **Noop Key** (internal/encryption/noop.go): A passthrough that stores data unencrypted (plaintext in = plaintext out). Used when encryption is explicitly set to 'noop' in config.\\n\\nSupporting primitives:\\n- **aeshelper** (internal/encryption/aeshelper/aeshelper.go): Raw AES-256-GCM encrypt/decrypt using crypto/rand nonces.\\n- **envelope** (internal/encryption/envelope/envelope.go): Envelope encryption — generates a random 32-byte key, encrypts plaintext with AES-GCM, returns (key, nonce, ciphertext) so the outer KMS only needs to protect a small key.\\n- **wrapper** (internal/encryption/wrapper/encryptedvalue.go): Serialization layer — `StorableEncryptedKey` struct (mechanism, key name, wrapped key, ciphertext, nonce) serialized as base64-encoded JSON for database storage.\\n- **cache** (internal/encryption/cache/cache.go): Optional LRU cache wrapper around any Key, memoizing decrypted values keyed by FNV-64 hash of ciphertext. Enabled by `EnableCache`/`CacheSize` in site config.\\n\\nThe **keyring** (internal/encryption/keyring/ring.go) is the global registry. The `Ring` struct holds one `encryption.Key` per sensitive data domain: `BatchChangesCredentialKey`, `ExternalServiceKey`, `GitHubAppKey`, `OutboundWebhookKey`, `UserExternalAccountKey`, `WebhookKey`, `WebhookLogKey`, `ExecutorSecretKey`, `SlackConfigurationKey`. Keys are configured in site config under `encryption.keys`. `keyring.Init()` watches for config changes and rebuilds the ring live; `keyring.Default()` provides global read access. `keyring.NewKey()` dispatches on key type (cloudkms/awskms/mounted/noop) to construct the appropriate backend.\\n\\nApplication code uses `Encryptable` (internal/encryption/encryptable.go) and `JSONEncryptable[T]` (internal/encryption/json_encryptable.go) wrappers for lazy, memoized encrypt/decrypt. `MaybeEncrypt`/`MaybeDecrypt` (internal/encryption/helpers.go) are nil-safe helpers: if `key == nil` (encryption disabled), `MaybeEncrypt` stores plaintext and `MaybeDecrypt` returns plaintext — this is the noop/disabled path. A special `ALLOW_DECRYPTION=true` env var suppresses new encryption during migration worker runs. Key mismatch is detected by comparing stored `encryption_key_id` (serialized `KeyVersion` JSON) against the current key's version on decryption.\\n\\n**Encrypted database fields** (cmd/worker/internal/encryption/encryption_tables.go):\\n- `external_services.config` → ExternalServiceKey\\n- `user_external_accounts.auth_data`, `account_data` → UserExternalAccountKey\\n- `user_credentials.credential` → BatchChangesCredentialKey\\n- `batch_changes_site_credentials.credential` → BatchChangesCredentialKey\\n- `webhook_logs.request`, `response` → WebhookLogKey\\n- `executor_secrets.value` → ExecutorSecretKey\\n- `outbound_webhooks.url`, `secret` → OutboundWebhookKey\\n- `slack_configurations.signing_secret`, `bot_token` → SlackConfigurationKey\\n\\nEach encrypted row stores both the ciphertext and an `encryption_key_id` column. Config validation (cmd/frontend/internal/conf/validation/encryption.go) calls `keyring.NewRing` at startup to surface misconfiguration errors early. RSA keys (internal/encryption/rsa.go) are used separately for SSH-based credential generation, not as an encryption backend in the keyring.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":3,"cache_creation_input_tokens":355,"cache_read_input_tokens":53337,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":355,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"71d5a283-c204-49e1-8811-ae5541ec87be","uuid":"d5837893-7372-47a2-8fc5-d87ff3c8d9ff"}

Four concrete backends implement this interface:\\n\\n1. **GCP Cloud KMS** (internal/encryption/cloudkms/cloud_kms.go): Uses Google Cloud KMS API with envelope encryption — a random AES-256 key encrypts the payload locally, then KMS wraps that envelope key.\\n2. **AWS KMS** (internal/encryption/awskms/aws_kms.go): Uses AWS KMS API with the same envelope pattern — AES-256-GCM local encryption with the envelope key protected by AWS KMS.\\n3. **Mounted Key** (internal/encryption/mounted/key.go): AES-256-GCM encryption using a 32-byte key loaded from an environment variable or filesystem path. Uses envelope encryption internally. This is the self-hosted/on-prem option.\\n4. **Noop Key** (internal/encryption/noop.go): A passthrough that stores data unencrypted (plaintext in = plaintext out). Used when encryption is explicitly set to 'noop' in config.\\n\\nSupporting primitives:\\n- **aeshelper** (internal/encryption/aeshelper/aeshelper.go): Raw AES-256-GCM encrypt/decrypt using crypto/rand nonces.\\n- **envelope** (internal/encryption/envelope/envelope.go): Envelope encryption — generates a random 32-byte key, encrypts plaintext with AES-GCM, returns (key, nonce, ciphertext) so the outer KMS only needs to protect a small key.\\n- **wrapper** (internal/encryption/wrapper/encryptedvalue.go): Serialization layer — `StorableEncryptedKey` struct (mechanism, key name, wrapped key, ciphertext, nonce) serialized as base64-encoded JSON for database storage.\\n- **cache** (internal/encryption/cache/cache.go): Optional LRU cache wrapper around any Key, memoizing decrypted values keyed by FNV-64 hash of ciphertext. Enabled by `EnableCache`/`CacheSize` in site config.\\n\\nThe **keyring** (internal/encryption/keyring/ring.go) is the global registry. The `Ring` struct holds one `encryption.Key` per sensitive data domain: `BatchChangesCredentialKey`, `ExternalServiceKey`, `GitHubAppKey`, `OutboundWebhookKey`, `UserExternalAccountKey`, `WebhookKey`, `WebhookLogKey`, `ExecutorSecretKey`, `SlackConfigurationKey`. Keys are configured in site config under `encryption.keys`. `keyring.Init()` watches for config changes and rebuilds the ring live; `keyring.Default()` provides global read access. `keyring.NewKey()` dispatches on key type (cloudkms/awskms/mounted/noop) to construct the appropriate backend.\\n\\nApplication code uses `Encryptable` (internal/encryption/encryptable.go) and `JSONEncryptable[T]` (internal/encryption/json_encryptable.go) wrappers for lazy, memoized encrypt/decrypt. `MaybeEncrypt`/`MaybeDecrypt` (internal/encryption/helpers.go) are nil-safe helpers: if `key == nil` (encryption disabled), `MaybeEncrypt` stores plaintext and `MaybeDecrypt` returns plaintext — this is the noop/disabled path. A special `ALLOW_DECRYPTION=true` env var suppresses new encryption during migration worker runs. Key mismatch is detected by comparing stored `encryption_key_id` (serialized `KeyVersion` JSON) against the current key's version on decryption.\\n\\n**Encrypted database fields** (cmd/worker/internal/encryption/encryption_tables.go):\\n- `external_services.config` → ExternalServiceKey\\n- `user_external_accounts.auth_data`, `account_data` → UserExternalAccountKey\\n- `user_credentials.credential` → BatchChangesCredentialKey\\n- `batch_changes_site_credentials.credential` → BatchChangesCredentialKey\\n- `webhook_logs.request`, `response` → WebhookLogKey\\n- `executor_secrets.value` → ExecutorSecretKey\\n- `outbound_webhooks.url`, `secret` → OutboundWebhookKey\\n- `slack_configurations.signing_secret`, `bot_token` → SlackConfigurationKey\\n\\nEach encrypted row stores both the ciphertext and an `encryption_key_id` column. Config validation (cmd/frontend/internal/conf/validation/encryption.go) calls `keyring.NewRing` at startup to surface misconfiguration errors early. RSA keys (internal/encryption/rsa.go) are used separately for SSH-based credential generation, not as an encryption backend in the keyring.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
